Soviet Troops Occupy Several Cities; Finnish Troops Retreat from Karelia; General Mannerheim Encourages Soldiers to Hold Their Ground; Finnish Foreign Minister Denies He Will Accompany the Prime Minister to London 21

Moscow – The Red Army announced last night that the Mannerheim Line, the main defense line of the Finnish army, was broken by Soviet troops yesterday, and the Red Army vowed to destroy all the enemy. According to the Red Army communique, the Red Army has broken through the first line of the Finnish army in the direction of Karelia, occupying one hundred and sixty-one strategic points, only twelve and a half miles from Vyborg. The communique stated that Finnish resistance on the Mannerheim Line was not intense, and most of them surrendered. The communique also stated that this decision by the Soviet army occupied the most fortified position of the Finnish army on the eastern line. (United Press dispatch of the 18th)

Moscow – According to a communique from the Leningrad Military District Headquarters, on the 17th, in the direction of Karelia, the enemy army retreated rapidly towards the Vamppula area under severe attack by the Soviet army, suffering heavy losses, and set fire to villages and towns along the way. The Soviet army has now occupied many important points, including the city of Ono, on the north bank of Lake Muolaa; the Sienno station, six kilometers southeast of Vamppula; the Kahula fortress area (west of Summa); and the coastal city of Naakka-Marila. In these areas, the Soviet army is pursuing the fleeing enemy troops. In other areas, there has been no significant development. The Soviet Air Force bombed enemy troops and enemy military targets. (TASS dispatch of the 18th)

Moscow – A communique released here last night stated that the Soviets have occupied the military stations of Leppiaesses and Kimmila and are continuing to advance. Yesterday, Soviet troops occupied twenty-two fortifications, and during several major offensives, seized forty-two machine guns and one hundred and seventy field guns. Soviet aircraft continued to bomb Finnish troops and military targets. Five Finnish aircraft were shot down. (Reuters dispatch of the 18th)

Helsinki – A communique released here last night acknowledged that the Finnish army in the Karelian Isthmus is now retreating, but stated that a team of Soviet ski troops near Kuhmo in central Finland has been dispersed. (Reuters dispatch of the 18th)

Helsinki – An air raid alarm was issued in Helsinki yesterday. Thirty Soviet bombers and fighters invaded the airspace, but did not drop bombs. The alarm was lifted half an hour later, and the Soviet aircraft immediately flew west, and it is expected that they will bomb places such as Tavastehus, Tammerfors, and Aboa. (Haitong dispatch of the 18th)

Stockholm – Telegrams between here and Finland were interrupted yesterday for a time and were restored after several hours. It is heard that an air raid alarm was issued in Helsinki. (Reuters dispatch of the 18th)

He believes that the Soviet army will definitely not be able to break through the Finnish defenses, and a considerable amount of foreign aid is now flowing in. From the overall situation, the hope of Finnish victory is increasing. (Reuters dispatch of the 18th)

The assistance given by foreign countries is quite considerable, and foreign volunteers are joining our army every day. It is time for us to stop the enemy's advance in the predetermined position. It should be known that there are other positions behind this position, and it is difficult for the enemy to advance to our last line of defense. If we continue to attack, we will only waste our forces. According to a reporter from the Dagens Nyheter newspaper in Stockholm, the intensity of the air raids suffered by Finland on Saturday and Sunday was unprecedented since the beginning of the war. More than 300 Soviet aircraft bombed 14 towns and cities outside the occupational zone, but there were few civilian casualties and the damage was very minor. (Reuters dispatch of the 18th)

London. Regarding the German auxiliary ship Altmark case, the Admiralty has just issued a second public statement, describing the search by the British destroyer Cossack, stating: "Our destroyer Cossack was ordered to sail to the mouth of Jøssingfjord in Norway, where it encountered two Norwegian gunboats. Captain Vian of the Cossack boarded the Norwegian gunboat and proposed to the captain that each side send several sailors to board the German ship Altmark and order it to sail to Bergen Port so that everything could be resolved in accordance with international law. However, the Norwegian captain refused, saying that he had received instructions from the government and was unable to do so, and provided assurances that the Altmark had been inspected twice in Norwegian ports and was not carrying British prisoners. After further negotiations, the Norwegian captain agreed to go to the Cossack and board the Altmark with a British officer. The Cossack then sent sailors to board the ship, and the two sides immediately opened fire. British leading soldier Miller was wounded. Our sailors then climbed onto the deck and drove the German captain out of the bridge. At this point, the ship was completely under our control. Our sailors immediately returned fire, killing two German soldiers, and another one fell into the sea. Two British officers also accidentally fell into the sea and were rescued. German Foreign Minister's Special Envoy Arrives in Japan to Conduct Diplomatic Activities - Schifferlich's Mission in Japan is to Examine the Current State of Relations Between the Two Countries 35

Tokyo - Schifferlich, manager of the German "Hamburg America Line," commissioned by the German Foreign Minister Ribbentrop, arrived here on the 13th of this month. His mission is to study the current status and future of German-Japanese relations. In the future, he will likely stay in Japan for several months as a special envoy of the German Foreign Minister. According to well-informed sources, the "Asama Maru" incident is the real motive for the German government to send a special envoy to Japan. Since the rapprochement between Germany and the Soviet Union in September of last year, not only have German-Japanese relations not developed much, but the Japanese people have also become very indifferent to Germany. The German diplomatic authorities are therefore very anxious. After the "Asama Maru" case was resolved, it was considered a major diplomatic failure, and the plan to promote Japan's accession to the Axis powers was also severely hit. Regarding the "Asama Maru" case, it is said that the German Foreign Ministry expressed dissatisfaction to Japanese Foreign Minister Arita, believing that the way the case was resolved showed that Japan was sacrificing German interests to promote pro-British policies. Moreover, Japanese shipping companies even exceeded the limits of government instructions and refused to carry any German passengers. In other words, they not only refused to carry Germans of military age, but also refused to carry any other passengers holding German citizenship. This is one reason. Secondly, the Japanese government prohibited nationals of belligerent countries from traveling from Japan to Korea on Japanese ships, making it increasingly difficult for German nationals to return home via the Siberian Railway. In view of this, the German government sent Schifferlich to Japan to investigate the truth. After returning to his country in the future, he will reportedly answer the following questions in a report: (1) Is there any possibility of further improving German-Japanese relations, and what is the best way to promote diplomatic relations? (2) How strong is the "pro-German element" among the Japanese leadership? (3) How will the relations between Japan and the Soviet Union affect German-Japanese relations? (4) How strong is the pro-British faction in Japan? (5) What are the prospects for the peace movement led by Wang Jingwei? (6) How will Japanese-American relations develop? In addition, Schifferlich will also study various economic issues to determine what kind of assistance Japan can provide to Germany and the Soviet Union in the future. At the same time, he also has orders from Foreign Minister Ribbentrop to investigate how much responsibility the current German Ambassador to Japan, General Ott, should bear for the coldness in German-Japanese relations. Some say that in addition to these things, Schifferlich will also take this opportunity to imply that Germany may be forced to revise its current Far East policy. In other words, Germany may restore its original policy pursued before 1938, that is, the policy of assisting General Chiang Kai-shek of China. The difference is that this time it will be done jointly with the Soviet Union. In short, it is generally said here that Schifferlich's trip shows that the German authorities are currently very anxious about the possibility of the scope of the European war expanding. Therefore, they still regard Japan as an important factor in the international situation in the coming months and are unwilling to ignore it. (Havas News Agency, 18th)

Japanese Troops Occupying Chao-Shan, Divergent Strategies of Navy and Army. Navy Insists on Holding the Position, Army Intends to Abandon 46

Shantou Correspondence: The death toll of Japanese troops occupying Chao-Shan is very significant. Last year, on October 15th, a memorial service was held at the Cheng Jing Shan She in Zhongma Road, Shantou, with 4,500 bags of wooden tablets and ashes of fallen soldiers lined up. Since November, the fighting outside Chao-Shan has not stopped for a single night. Battles took place in Anbu, Sangyoupu Mountain, Niaotagang, Pan'nan Mountain, Jiao Mountain, Huamei, Hong'an Village, Guanchao, Jinshi, Fuyang, Yunbu, Fengxi, Xitang, Xucu Long, Xiangtou Village, Zhuyuan, Chihu, Xia Temple, Tonghu, Guxiang, Qiulang Mountain, Zhulong Mountain, and Bijia Mountain. The casualties of Japanese troops in these battles are estimated to be over four to five thousand. Since the landing of Japanese soldiers in Shantou on June 11th last year, almost 90% of the original force have died. The Japanese troops currently occupying Chao-Shan are all replacements successively drawn from Taiwan, Shanghai, and Guangzhou, without a single complete battalion. According to the observation of Japanese military strategy, Chao-Shan was not originally a major battlefield. It is said that the Japanese army, due to heavy losses, has long had the intention of abandoning it. However, the Japanese navy attaches great importance to Chao-Shan, considering Shantou as a stronghold that must be defended in the navy's southward strategy. It also has significant economic blockade implications, which can isolate eight million overseas Chinese and shake their support for the anti-Japanese war. Given the different viewpoints of the Japanese army and navy on Chao-Shan, last autumn, Huang Dawei, the pseudo "Commander-in-Chief of the First Peace and National Salvation Army Group," set up a pseudo headquarters in Po Hai Cheng with the aim of capturing Fudai. Huang's actions only received support from Rear Admiral Takasu Shiro of the Japanese Navy's South China Fleet. The Japanese army in Chao-Shan did not sympathize. On November 25th, Huang's puppet army attacked Zhao'an along Long, Xiaodong, Huanggang, and Zhelin. The Japanese naval landing force landed along the coast to provide cover, so they were able to quickly break into the territory of Zhao'an. Later, because the Japanese army in Shantou did not feign an attack on Raoping City to cover the coastal line (Provincial Highway No. 1), the puppet troops of Huanggang and Zhelin were cut off by the army and people of Raoping. Lin Zhiyuan was captured in Dagang Township (Zhelin). Only a few of Huang's puppet troops escaped by sea. Those who escaped fled with their guns to Liangshan, at the border of Yunxiao and Tanpu, and more than 700 surrendered to Song Tiancai's division. Since Lin Zhiyuan was sent to Chongqing, several hundred more have surrendered after receiving letters from Lin and being pacified. Huang Dawei returned to Chenghai in defeat, became depressed, fell ill, and vomited blood. Last month, the Japanese army held a military meeting in Zhongshan Park in Shantou City. Huang fell ill in Bo'ai Hospital and did not attend. It is rumored that Huang has died of illness. It is said that when Huang was in Shanghai, the Japanese army promised to allocate one million yuan, 15,000 rifles, cannons, vehicles, speedboats, etc., and had the right to mobilize the Japanese army to assist in the battle. Unexpectedly, Huang was completely disappointed upon arriving in Chenghai, receiving only 3,000 rifles and over 200,000 yuan in military expenses, and the Japanese army did not provide assistance. In mid-January, the Japanese army in Chao-Shan held a military meeting. The army advocated advancing towards Jieyang and Fengshun to respond to the battle in northern Guangdong, while the navy advocated advancing towards Ping and the Fujian border to consolidate the periphery of the Chao-Shan occupied area and obtain sufficient supplies of grain, rice, oil, and salt to ensure Shantou as a key point. On January 20th, the Japanese navy again assisted Huang Dawei in attacking Donglong Lianyang, which was gained and then lost. The Japanese army attacked Fengxi, Xitang, and Qiulang Mountain along various lines, also resulting in disastrous defeats. At this point, the Japanese army in Chao-Shan began to change its strategy and switch to a defensive posture, with the goal of securing the eastern Fujian border and ensuring Shantou, Chenghai, Raoping, and Aonan as its future objectives. Starting on the 8th of this month, they have increased the defensive fortifications along the Chao-Shan Railway and secretly transferred the Chao-Cheng puppet peace army to warships. On the 9th, there were seven Japanese transport ships in Shantou Port. For a time, rumors spread in the city that the Japanese puppets were about to abandon Chao-Shan. In the early morning of the 10th, part of the military supplies from Aonan were unloaded at Qianjiang and sailed towards the South Fujian sea area. On the 11th, there were another forty to fifty large and small ships in the Dongshan Island area of Zhao'an. At noon on the 11th, Huang Dawei's puppet army landed near Hutou Mountain. The local militia briefly resisted and then retreated. With the cover of Japanese aircraft, 1,500 puppet soldiers advanced rapidly towards Zhangpu and Yunxiao, with the aim of attacking Zhangzhou. According to the Japanese navy's strategy, they want to link Zhangzhou and Xiamen together and establish a puppet government in Chao-Shan, Zhangzhou, and Xiamen to realize their cunning scheme of dividing China.

Educational News

Ministry of Education Promulgates Guidelines for Moral Education in Schools at All Levels (II) 48

2. Primary School

(1) Specific plans for training children should be formulated based on Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings, the Boy Scout training method, the New Life Movement rules, and the standards for civic training in primary schools.

(2) Attention should be paid to the integration of moral education and teaching, and the actual situation of life and the environment should be considered to connect schools with families and society.

(3) All faculty members of primary schools should jointly bear the responsibility of training, ensuring that attention is paid to children's various activities at all times and in all places, directly and indirectly using the rules and items of primary school civic training to guide children's behavior.

(4) Through the study of history and geography and the holding of various commemorative meetings, the spirit of loving the country and the nation should be inspired in children, and their enthusiasm, responsibility, public spirit, and virtues of doing good should be cultivated.

(5) Telling stories of national humiliation and national martyrs to inspire children's courage to avenge national humiliation and strengthen the country, as well as the spirit of loyalty, courage, and sacrifice.

(6) Through the narration of the words and deeds of Dr. Sun Yat-sen and President Chiang Kai-shek, children's respect and faith in the leaders should be established, and their virtues of loyalty, obedience, contribution, and sacrifice should be cultivated.

(7) Through the provision of practical knowledge in daily life, children's interest in learning and habits of scientific exploration should be aroused, and their virtues of diligence, meticulousness, modesty, questioning, careful consideration, clear discernment, and perseverance should be cultivated.

(8) Through the implementation of labor education, games, sports, and extracurricular activities, children's interest in production and labor should be inspired, and their spirit of agility, vitality, diligence, and dedication should be cultivated.

(9) Guidance on training in consumer cooperation and savings should be provided to develop children's habits of thrift and a spirit of mutual assistance and cooperation.

(10) Through school health and young children's training, habits of neatness, cleanliness, and hard work should be developed.

(11) Special training such as fire prevention, first aid, alarms, light control, traffic control, and evacuation drills should be held to make children understand the state of wartime so that they can be prepared.

(12) Through the study of music, art, etc., children's sentiments should be cultivated, and they should be given more contact with nature to develop their aesthetic sense.

(13) Practicing sweeping, answering, advancing, retreating, etc., to familiarize children with the etiquette of dealing with people, handling affairs, and receiving objects, so as to develop feelings of filial piety, respect, friendship, and harmony.

(14) Guiding children to organize class meetings and autonomous groups so that children can practice the rudiments of democracy and understand the application of the four powers.

(15) Training through group sports, gatherings, etc., to develop children's habits of punctuality and discipline.

(16) Arrange a hygienic environment, display slogans about public morality in public places, and guide the practice methods to develop children's virtues of paying attention to public health and cherishing public property.

Appendix: Standards for Civic Training in Primary Schools 49

Based on the needs of national construction, promote inherent morality and national spirit, formulate these standards, train children to develop healthy citizens who uphold the Three Principles of the People. The goals are as follows:

(1) Regarding citizens' physical training: Develop habits of exercise and hygiene, and a spirit of happiness and enterprise, so as to be able to defend oneself and the country.

(2) Regarding citizens' moral training: Develop concepts of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame, and virtues of love and sincerity, so as to be able to have self-confidence and believe in the Way.

(3) Regarding citizens' economic training: Develop habits of thrift and labor, and knowledge and skills in production and cooperation, so as to be able to support oneself and nurture others.

(4) Regarding citizens' political training: Develop concepts of public service and law-abiding, and ideas of loving the country and the community, so as to be able to govern oneself and manage affairs.

First Wish and Regulations

1. Wish (Lyrics)

I wish to abide by the regulations of Chinese citizens, to cultivate my character,

To strengthen my body, to improve my morality.

I wish to abide by the regulations of Chinese citizens, to establish my determination,

To produce and serve for the public, to fight for survival for the country.

I wish to be a good citizen of China, a good citizen of China,

To uphold the Three Principles of the People, and to advance towards the world of great harmony, forward, forward.

2. Regulations

(1) A Chinese citizen is strong: I keep my body, clothes, food, and residence clean, and pay attention to nutrition, exercise, and abide by the rules of the New Life Movement to keep my body strong.

(2) A Chinese citizen is happy: I am happy in spirit, lively in attitude, and can share happiness with everyone.

(3) A Chinese citizen is diligent: I love learning, do things conscientiously, am willing to work and prepare for creation, and have perseverance.

(4) A Chinese citizen is thrifty: I save money, cherish items, and pay attention to saving.

(5) A Chinese citizen is honest: I tell the truth, do practical things, and do not deceive myself or others.

(6) A Chinese citizen is prudent: I strive to be agile in all my actions, such as reading and doing things, and carefully observe and precisely distinguish between right and wrong.

(7) A Chinese citizen is responsible: I must do what I should do and do my best to do it well. Even if I encounter difficulties, I will not abandon my responsibility.

(8) A Chinese citizen is loyal and courageous: I strive to unite and defend, am not afraid of any difficulties, love the country, and do not care about any sacrifices.

(9) A Chinese citizen is filial and respectful: I am filial to my parents, respect my teachers, obey my leaders, listen to the teachings of my parents, teachers, and leaders, and abide by the resolutions of the group.

(10) A Chinese citizen is benevolent: I love my brothers and sisters, get along with my neighbors and relatives, help my compatriots at home and friends abroad, and help those in disaster and the disabled, and protect animals that are harmless to people.

(11) A Chinese citizen is courteous: I am not rude or arrogant, am polite to everyone and everything, and abide by all the etiquette that should be observed.

(12) A Chinese citizen is benevolent: I am enthusiastic about public welfare, like to serve the public, and will never damage public property, waste public land, or hinder the public.

(13) A Chinese citizen is honest: I do not take what I should not take, and I do not do things that harm others to benefit myself.

(14) A Chinese citizen knows shame: I will not allow myself and the country to suffer any shame. If I do, I will definitely find a way to wash it away.

(15) A Chinese citizen is productive: I learn productive knowledge and skills, strive to increase production, and seek welfare for the public.

(16) A Chinese citizen is mutually supportive: I help others and unite with the public to help each other, jointly produce and consume, in order to achieve the goal of common ownership, common governance, and common enjoyment.

(17) A Chinese citizen serves the public and abides by the law: I abide by the rules of the group and the laws of the country, and fulfill my due obligations and enjoy the rights I should enjoy.

(18) A Chinese citizen loves the country and the community: I love my group, my country, and my nation, and I am determined to work hard for the group.

Chang Lu flies to save, but it brushes the tip of his finger and bounces off the left post into the net. Opening the ball in the middle line, the final whistle sounds, Lido wins 3-1.

After the Signing of the Police Agreement, Various Circles Have Different Views; Foreigners Are Not Enthusiastic, While Chinese People Are Disappointed; There Are Many Difficulties Regarding Funding and Organization 58

The "North-China Daily News" reported that Major Bowen, Commissioner of the Shanghai Municipal Police, will hold a meeting with Lu Ying, the "Director of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau," in the next few days to discuss the detailed organization of the special new police force in the Western District, which was agreed upon by the Shanghai Municipal Council and the "Municipal Government." The location of the team's office has not yet been determined.

Police Force Organization Still Awaiting Negotiation

According to "Mayor" Fu Xiao'an's statement to reporters, the organization of the joint new police force will be discussed at a meeting to be held in the next few days. However, the date of the meeting has not yet been decided. The "Municipal Government" will use the income from the Western District to develop the area. Regarding the transfer of funds to banks, it is said that he has not yet discussed financial issues in detail with the Shanghai Municipal Council authorities.

Huge Sums Have Been Spent on Development of the Western District

When reporters mentioned that the Shanghai Municipal Council authorities had spent huge sums of money developing public interest projects in the Western District, Fu said that when this issue is raised for discussion, he will request to see the profit and loss statement, meaning that he will conduct a detailed review of the Shanghai Municipal Council authorities' income and expenditures.

New Police Officers Number 1,200

Also, the "Shanghai Times" reported that since the agreement on the special police force in the Shanghai Western Extra-Settlement Roads Area was signed on Friday, there has been much speculation in the city yesterday (the 17th) regarding the number of personnel and the general organization of the force. Although there has been no direct discussion between the two parties on this matter, it is heard from reliable sources that the new police force will consist of approximately 1,200 officers and constables. Based on the size of the area under the force's jurisdiction, it is expected that four police stations will be established in the district.

Searching for Police Station Buildings Will Take Time

The agreement signed by Fessenden, Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Council, and "Mayor of Shanghai" Fu Xiao'an, stipulates that the number and organization of the new police force shall be handled by the "Director of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau" and the Commissioner of the Shanghai Municipal Police. After the establishment of the special police force, it will have the exclusive right to operate in the Extra-Settlement Roads Area during the term of the agreement. However, it is expected that the organization of the police force cannot be completed in a short period of time, as in addition to selecting police officers and constables, there is also the issue of finding suitable buildings in the area to serve as police stations.

Separate Regulations for Police Officer Insignia

A key feature of the agreement signed on Friday is that the special police force is established by the "Municipal Government" and wears distinctive shoulder badges or insignias, and has exclusive powers in the district. The organization of the police force personnel will be determined by the Commissioner of the Shanghai Municipal Police and the "Director of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau."

Personnel Selection Awaits Consultation

According to the provisional terms, a portion of the police force members, including some key officers, shall be appointed by the "Shanghai Municipal Government" from candidates recommended by the Shanghai Municipal Council. Undoubtedly, after consultation between the Commissioner of the Shanghai Municipal Police and the Deputy Commissioner, it will take a long time to submit a list of Shanghai Municipal Police officers. If these police officers are approved by the "Shanghai Municipal Government," they will be assigned to the special police force. It is heard that the police force commander will be appointed by Fu Xiao'an, while the deputy commander will be appointed by the Shanghai Municipal Police.

Police Officers' Benefits and Privileges to Be Retained

One of the terms of the agreement stipulates that "The head of the police station in the area where foreigners have large properties, and a number of officers determined through agreement, shall be appointed by the "Shanghai Municipal Government" from candidates recommended by the Shanghai Municipal Council." The future of these Shanghai Municipal Police officers will then become an issue, as they will still expect to retain all rights and privileges when assigned to the special police force, such as promotions during their service in the Shanghai Municipal Police. Their salaries in the special police force will also be comparable to those in the Shanghai Municipal Police.

Detective Agency To Be Organized Separately

In addition, there are various other issues that need to be decided. Although there has not been much progress in the discussion of various plans to date, it is generally expected that Shanghai Municipal Police officers assigned to the special police force will still be considered Shanghai Municipal Police personnel and have full rights and privileges. After the establishment of the special police force, it will soon establish its own detective division, which will fully cooperate with the Shanghai Municipal Police and the "Municipal Police Bureau."

Chinese and Foreign Views Differ

Also, the "China Press" reported that the reactions of people in the city to the agreement between the Shanghai Municipal Council and the "Shanghai Municipal Government" on police affairs in the Extra-Settlement Roads Area yesterday were varied. Foreigners generally approve of the agreement in principle, but do not express great enthusiasm, and generally believe that the agreement is a step in the right direction on paper. However, foreigners also feel skeptical and believe it is best to wait and see how the words can be translated into action. As for the Chinese, although they acknowledge that the agreement may solve the problem of crime in the city, they say that the "Shanghai Municipal Government" may interpret the Shanghai Municipal Council's willingness to sign the agreement as a de facto recognition of the puppet regime, which is regrettable.

The Japanese Side Is Very Pleased

Only the reaction from the Japanese side has been absolutely welcoming of the agreement, calling it a historical document and congratulating the Shanghai Municipal Council and the "Municipal Government" on signing the agreement. As for the reaction of the Shanghai Municipal Council, it is not yet known. It is heard that since the Shanghai Municipal Council believes that it is appropriate to sign the agreement, it will naturally approve it. However, it is claimed that no matter how the "Municipal Government" treats the agreement thereafter, it will not be detrimental to the Shanghai Municipal Council. There are now two possibilities: (1) If the "Municipal Government" cooperates in accordance with the provisions of the agreement, it will be beneficial to the public interest; (2) If the "Municipal Government" refuses to comply with the terms of the agreement, it will permanently prove that the "Municipal Government" has no sincerity, and the unstable situation should be entirely blamed on the "Municipal Government."

The Goal of Price Stabilization Is Persistence; Request for Statutory Foreign Exchange; Worried Because the Compensation Funds Are Still Not Enough; Rice Prices at Retail Stores Have Not Fallen, Hope for Strict Punishment 59

The Shanghai Price Stabilization Committee decided to implement the second phase of price stabilization from February 23rd. The Rice Merchants Association has passed a resolution to accept the entrustment to handle it, stipulating that 40 price stabilization locations will be set up in the two settlements. The locations will be announced after the Rice Merchants Association decides. All procedures are being rushed to ensure implementation as scheduled. Regarding the time of price stabilization, it has been changed to run from 1:30 PM to 6:00 PM until sold out. Each location will stabilize the price of 50 bags per day. Each person is limited to purchasing one yuan, which is equivalent to 5.5 catties, which is half a catty less than the first phase.

Request for the Supply of Statutory Foreign Exchange

The 15th, 30th, and 6th branch associations of the Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Union, in view of the food difficulties last year, after negotiating with Yu Qiaqing and others, initiated the purchase of foreign rice and were approved to supply statutory foreign exchange to regulate the situation temporarily. The benevolence was widely received and Shanghai was grateful. Now the problem of people's food is severe, and the situation is even worse than in the past. Citizens are starving and crises are lurking. The People's Food Regulation Association, although organizing price stabilization, is limited by its financial resources and cost relations, and it is still difficult to reverse the current situation. Therefore, it has specially sent a letter to the People's Food Association, requesting it to earnestly present to the National Government authorities to invoke the previous example and specially approve statutory foreign exchange for Shanghai's future stabilization of foreign rice prices in order to relieve the poor people's suffering and suppress the rising prices.

Continuing Fundraising for Persistent Price Stabilization

The Price Stabilization Committee previously stipulated that the price stabilization donation fund was 1 million yuan in national currency. After enthusiastic donations from various industries and social donations, the total amount of donations received has reached 567,459 yuan and 4 jiao and 3 fen. There is still a long way to go to reach the goal. The association continues to raise funds to ensure that it reaches the 1 million yuan goal so that price stabilization can be sustained. It is heard that various industries have decided to continue to apportion the funds. As for the agencies that receive donations, they are still Shanghai Jin Cheng, Fu Yuan, Tong Run, and other banks and businesses. In addition, the association has purchased approximately 80,000 bags of broken rice. In addition to the 34,000 bags sold in the first phase, there are still 46,000 bags remaining.

Rice Prices Have Fallen Back, But Retail Prices Have Not

More than 500 rice stores in the city closed down the day before yesterday for fear of being robbed by civilians, and have not yet reopened yesterday. However, retail sales continued as usual. The market was sluggish, so prices have fallen back again. It is estimated that No. 1 Saigon Tokyo fell 8 jiao per tip, while grain rice fell about 1 yuan each, and Bai Yuan fell about 1.5 yuan each. Danyang white rice fell even more, dropping 2 yuan. However, the retail prices of rice stores have not decreased, and it is hoped that the relevant authorities will impose strict sanctions.

A Rice Riot Occurred in Pudong

Although the price of domestic rice in Pudong District differs from the settlements by more than 10 yuan, the highest price has reached 40 yuan per picul. Starting yesterday, the rice stores also unanimously hoarded goods, hiding good rice and only selling broken rice in stores, also at 40 yuan per dan. The general poor people were greatly panicked. At 9 AM, a rice riot occurred at Yanjiabao, on the border of Shangnan. At that time, Yuanchang Rice Store on Dongchang Road went to Zhoupu to purchase 48 bags of rice. On the way back, when passing through Yanjiabao, hundreds of poor people completely robbed all the rice. In the afternoon, hundreds of poor people also robbed rice stores in Xitangqiao and other towns in the south. At 2 PM in Yangjiadu Town, 500-600 poor people gathered, holding rice baskets and flour bags, and were preparing to rob rice when they were suppressed and dispersed by Japanese troops. If rice prices continue to rise, a more serious wave of unrest will be triggered in the suburbs of Shanghai.

The Coal Briquette Industry Has Resolved to Implement Price Stabilization Tomorrow; Wholesale Price Is 110 Yuan per Dan, 5.8 Yuan; Limited to Clearing Warehouse Receipts within 10 Days, Overdue Receipts Will Be Canceled 60

The Shanghai Coal Briquette Industry Association and the Bean and Rice Industry Association yesterday received a letter from Wu Shaoshu, Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters, ordering them to suppress and stabilize the prices of rice and coal briquettes, and stating that rice is a necessity for people's food and coal briquettes are a daily necessity for fuel. Now that market prices have soared, it is related to the livelihoods of 3 million citizens and they are ordered to suppress and stabilize prices. If hoarding and price gouging occur, once verified, they will be dealt with according to law.

All Sectors Negotiate to Suppress Coal Prices

Leaders from all walks of life, such as Yu Qiaqing, Xu Jiyi, and Lin Kanghou, especially invited Chen Cuifang, Chairman of the Coal Briquette Industry Association, and representatives from various coal briquette factories the day before yesterday to discuss ways to maintain fuel for the common people. It was decided on the spot that: (1) Openly stipulate a unified coal briquette price; (2) Limit the time for hoarders to clear their warehouse receipts (the above are temporary measures); (3) Find ways to reduce freight for coal dust needed by various factories (this is a fundamental solution). According to the current factory price, based on current costs, it is said that it is still less than the cost.

Coal Briquette Price Stabilization Will Be Implemented Tomorrow

The Machine-Made Coal Briquette Industry Association convened a joint meeting of various manufacturers at 4 PM yesterday. Representatives from 18 companies, including Yitaixing, Guohua, Jingye, and Dongfang, attended. After Chairman Chen Cuifang reported the purpose of the meeting, it was resolved on the spot that: (1) Starting from the 20th of this month (i.e., tomorrow), price stabilization will be implemented. The retail price will be 5.8 yuan per 100-catty dan, and the wholesale price will be 110 yuan per ton, with an additional 2 yuan for labor; (2) Negotiate with the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to publish a notice in the newspaper that customer warehouse receipts must be delivered within 10 days, otherwise they will be taken back at the original price and no goods will be delivered.

Coal Reserves Reach One Million Tons

A reporter from the New Voice News Agency approached Mr. Bao Xixiang, a member of the Coal Industry Committee, yesterday to inquire about the coal reserves in Shanghai and ways to suppress market prices. According to Mr. Bao, there is no shortage of fuel in Shanghai as a whole. Coal scraps from Annam and other places arrive every day. Although there are many uses at present, the coal stockpiled in Shanghai East and West warehouses has reached more than 1 million tons, which is enough for 4 million Shanghai citizens to use for one and a half years. It is clear that the rising market prices are caused by manipulation and monopoly. To suppress market prices, it is essential to purchase in large quantities, reduce freight costs, and urge existing inventory to be released from warehouses. This will result in a glut of spot coal, a balance of supply and demand, and falling market prices.

Hoping the Authorities Thoroughly Investigate Hoarding

Mr. Xiong continued, "The soaring price of coal in Shanghai is not only related to the entire industry, but also poses a serious threat to the livelihoods of ordinary people. Although the members of the association are aware of this situation, they are ultimately unable to do anything due to their lack of resources and energy. It is hoped that the authorities of both settlements will promptly send personnel to conduct a thorough investigation of coal reserves, urge the release of goods from warehouses, and sell them at stable prices in order to stabilize coal prices. It is heard that the Fuel Committee of the Settlements is paying close attention to the rising coal prices and convened a committee meeting the day before yesterday afternoon to discuss countermeasures. Therefore, the overall fuel problem in Shanghai can be gradually stabilized. It is hoped that citizens will remain calm and not privately purchase and hoard, so as to avoid reducing existing inventory.

I cannot reply to all the letters from all sectors here, so I would like to express my gratitude here."

Stores Use Fractional Currency for Change; The Fifth Batch of Fractional Currency Coupons Will Be Issued Today; Substitute Coupons Are No Longer Accepted 62

Since the Central Bank issued fractional currency, the total amount has reached 2 million yuan, and a large amount of it has been circulated in the market. The fifth batch of 500,000 yuan has been scheduled to be issued starting today. At present, various stores in the city mainly use tram substitute coupons, bus tokens, and coupons from the four major companies in the two settlements for change. Now that the fifth batch of fractional currency coupons has been scheduled to be issued starting today, the shortage of auxiliary currency can be gradually eliminated. Fufeng and Fuxin Supply Flour; Stabilized Prices Will Be Implemented Starting Today; Noodle Shops Will Temporarily Close Starting Today; Representatives Will Be Sent to the Chamber of Commerce to Petition for Relief 63

In order to maintain people's food and relieve the poor, the flour factory industry has decided to designate 27 flour stores in the two settlements to be responsible for implementing stabilized prices for one month. Fufeng and Fuxin will supply the flour, providing 7,500 bags per day, including 5,000 bags of Fufeng "Red and Blue Car Brand" and 2,500 bags of Fuxin "Red Fuxin Brand." Each bag weighs 49 pounds.

All will be sold at the stabilized price of 10 yuan and 3 jiao. The factory wholesale price is 10 yuan, and the retail price is increased by 3 jiao for handling fees. Each person is limited to purchasing one bag at a time. 27 flour stores, including Ruiji, have already received goods from Fufeng and Fuxin yesterday and will implement stabilized prices starting today. The order of the price stabilization stores will be maintained by the police department of the settlement authorities. The price stabilization time is from 9 AM to 12 PM and from 2 PM until sold out. Only other brands of flour will not be sold during the price stabilization period.

Machine-Made Noodle Shops Decide to Close

In view of the soaring price of flour, the Shanghai Machine-Made Noodle Industry Association held a temporary members' meeting yesterday morning and decided to temporarily close down starting today (the 19th) with pain. It is heard that starting today, more than 200 noodle shops, including Zhu Daxing, Wang Yuanlong, and Wang Maoxing, in the Public and French Concessions will temporarily close down.

Petition the Chamber of Commerce for Relief

The association's official document to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday stated, "This is to petition for the skyrocketing price and shortage of flour. The association convened a temporary emergency meeting yesterday. The members from various markets in the city reported that they had no goods to make and were forced to decide to suspend business with pain on February 19th. We are deeply afraid that the authorities will question us, so we are submitting this report to your association in advance, begging you to transfer it to the authorities to dredge the source, negotiate with manufacturers to directly supply the association, and then distribute it to the members in the market according to a fixed quota. The association will register with each store and is responsible for managing the goods, and hoarding is not allowed. The association is responsible for handling it. Please also ask the authorities to limit the price of flour to no more than 10 yuan and quickly handle the foreign wheat to relieve the flour shortage and benefit the business, so as to benefit the people's food.

Prices are rising, and the entire city of Shanghai is shaken by it. Employees who are paid salaries are already on the verge of not being able to maintain their livelihoods. Able-Bodied Men on Shanghai-Hangzhou Trains Are Always Driven Off 69

Every Station Has a "Draft Team"; Trains Are Always Searched Strictly

That is, a "draft team" is set up at every railway station. If any strong and able-bodied Chinese are found, they are forced to be taken to a certain place to listen to their commands, share the burden of transportation and construction work, and are whipped if they are not careful. In addition, in order to prevent Chinese guerrillas from mixing in, the Japanese army has been strictly checking train passengers, often hindering the train's running time. Every train that passes through must be harshly searched by the Japanese army. Anyone who is strong and able-bodied or is suspected is taken away. Therefore, the early train on the Shanghai-Hangzhou line, which departed from Wangdian yesterday, departed at 9:15 AM and was supposed to arrive in Shanghai at around 12:00 noon, but when the train passed Jiashan, the Japanese army forced passengers to get off the train for inspection for two hours, and five Chinese people were taken away. The train did not arrive at the Shanghai North Station until 2 PM.

The Situation in Tianjin Is Tragic; What a Major Foreign Merchant Said After Arriving in Shanghai; The Golden Age of the Past Is Nowhere to Be Found 70

The "China Press" reported that a major merchant from Tianjin recently arrived in Shanghai. He told reporters yesterday (the 17th) that he has been traveling in Tianjin for 35 years and has never seen the situation as bad as it is today. Unless the current situation changes, he does not know how foreign businessmen can continue to exist. Foreign business firms are gradually disappearing.

Coal Is as Expensive as Gold, Rice Shortages Are Even Worse

The Japanese in Tianjin are doing everything they can to make it extremely difficult for businessmen to operate. Now, most foreigners are reminiscing about the prosperous times before the war. Before the Lunar New Year, Tianjin was very cold, and the situation was made worse by the coal shortage. Coal prices once soared, as expensive as gold. When he set off for Shanghai, the weather had warmed up, but rice and grain were also very scarce in Tianjin.

The Japanese Compiled Shandong Tobacco

Foreign tobacco companies that used to import large quantities of tobacco from Shandong can no longer do so. If they want to import, they must purchase from a company managed by the Japanese. However, the tobacco obtained is less in quantity and inferior in quality than what was ordered. Sometimes, when ordering first-class tobacco, they receive third-class goods. Those who have connections with the company have priority in obtaining first-class tobacco, which is very unfair.

All Kinds of Food Are Very Scarce

All kinds of food in Tianjin, especially perishable food, are still very scarce. Large companies in the settlements have to rent trucks to transport food into the settlements themselves. The rental fee for trucks is 15 or 20 yuan per hour. They are searched along the way, causing delays for several hours. Even if the food does not spoil during the period of being stopped, the rent for the trucks that the company spends is already very expensive. Due to the high cost of transporting food, food in the settlements is half as expensive as outside the settlements. Regarding the "Federal Reserve" banknotes, their value may continue to fall within the next week.

take off their hats and salute

violently beaten and injured

by Japanese soldiers with iron and wooden sticks, rifle butts, etc. The day before yesterday afternoon, several Chinese women were beaten in the head and bled profusely because they did not know how to salute. Many other men were also beaten and injured, with their heads bleeding. Therefore, yesterday, the number of pedestrians on the bridge decreased compared to the previous few days. stopped by Japanese soldiers

and forced to salute when he passed through the New Zha Bridge from the concession to Zhabei because he did not take off his hat. The British man refused and turned back to the concession. It is now known that the bridge has been slightly repaired, so it has been opened to traffic as usual since yesterday. Previously, only one iron gate on the east side was opened, but now both the east and west sides are fully open.

Fear of Permanent Disability

US Transport Ship USS Chaumont's Relationship with the Shanghai War, The First Naval Reinforcements Arrive in Shanghai 73

— Xiu Quan

The USS Chaumont, one of the six major transport ships of the United States Navy, was ordered by the Navy Department on November 3, 1921, to sail between the Far East and the Pearl Harbor Naval Base in San Francisco, USA. Now that it has been in service for nineteen years, it is about to leave the Far Eastern waters and return to its home in the United States. There are many things worth mentioning about the ship's history with the Shanghai War, so the following is a brief summary:

The USS Chaumont was built in Hog Island, eastern United States, in 1920 and is one of the six major transport ships of the United States Navy. The ship weighs 11,000 tons, is 448 feet long, and 58 feet wide. In the same year, the US Navy Department built six transport ships of the same class in Hog Island, which only took 19 days to sail from the United States to the Far East. There are also two sister ships: one is the USS Accony, which is dedicated to carrying food and military supplies, and the other is the USS Ryder, which is used to transport ammunition, airplanes, tanks, and artillery. The USS Chaumont joined the Far East voyage in 1921. On August 6, 1924, after completing the work tasks of the Navy Department headquarters, it was ordered to sail to the Norfolk waters of Virginia, and then it would come to the Far East twice a year. The USS Chaumont once carried US Navy personnel to Haiti and transferred to Guantanamo Bay Naval Base in western Cuba, West Indies, for service. From there, it sailed to the Panama Canal, stayed overnight, and passed through the Atlantic Ocean to the Pacific Ocean, and then turned from the Bell Department to San Diego.

The USS Chaumont was stationed between San Diego, St. Paul, and San Francisco, and it was responsible for transportation matters in the Far East, including Honolulu, Guam, Manila, Hong Kong, Shanghai, Qingdao, and Qin Island in the Pacific Ocean. The first time the USS Chaumont arrived in Shanghai was in 1927, when the National Revolutionary Army had just conquered Shanghai. At that time, the USS Chaumont was on alert in Nicaragua because of a conflict between the local important official Sandino and the US Navy. It was then ordered by the Navy Department to rush to Shanghai to strengthen the defense of the concession. This was on February 24, 1927. On March 21, it returned to the United States and came to Shanghai again to protect the voyage of the President Pierce, which carried the commander of the US Fourth Naval Fleet to Shanghai.

The US Navy's second deployment to Shanghai was also carried out by the USS Chaumont, which arrived on February 5, 1932, when the "January 28" Shanghai War broke out. The ship was ordered to carry US Navy personnel from Manila to Shanghai to strengthen the defense of the concession. When the "August 13" Shanghai War broke out in 1937, the USS Chaumont once again carried personnel from the US Navy's Sixth Detachment and Brigadier General Simon Dewitt Buckner Jr. of the US Navy's Second Brigade to Shanghai. During that voyage, the USS Chaumont broke its previous voyage record and departed from San Diego fully loaded with military supplies and naval personnel on August 29 of that year, arriving in Shanghai on September 19 in 21 days. After the sudden outbreak of the August 13 Shanghai War, the USS Chaumont helped American expatriates in Yantai, Qingdao, and Tianjin evacuate to Shanghai, and carried some expatriates back to their home country via Kobe, Japan. Later, it sailed to Shanghai again and carried American expatriates to Hong Kong. The USS Chaumont performed more arduous tasks in the US Navy Department, and its achievements far surpassed those of other transport ships. Even on the way to the Far East, the ship helped other US ships that were damaged by storms. On December 16, 1936, when the USS Chaumont was six kilometers away from the sea off Qinhuangdao, it worked hard to help the USS Gold Star rescue the US Navy personnel who were in distress there and bring them to Shanghai. It is reported that the US Navy Department, considering that it has served in the Far East for 19 years, will recall it to San Diego, USA, and replace it with two other US transport ships. This will be seen in August next year. As for the US transport ship USS Henderson, which left Shanghai on January 28, it will still sail to Shanghai in the near future to strengthen the defense.

Only Son Tragically Crushed to Death 74

Children Playing in the Road

Parents Should Be Vigilant

Zhu Gengshou, a Suzhou boy living at No. 5 Yufu Lane, Kangdi Road, is 15 years old and an only child. His father died when he was five years old. His mother, Ms. Wang (45 years old this year), relied on her ten fingers to work as a female worker to raise him. At 5:30 p.m. on the 15th, while playing with other children in front of No. 557 Beile Road, an empty truck with the license plate F-257, driven by Zhao Honggui (39 years old) from Tongzhou, was driving slowly from south to north. Zhu and the other children were pushing and teasing the truck from behind when Zhu accidentally tripped and fell to the ground and his head was crushed by the rear wheel. The police saw this and rushed him to Guangci Hospital, but he died before he could be treated. The police took the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall autopsy room. The next day, they reported it to the prosecutor of the Second Special Court, who came to the scene to verify the cause of death. The police also sent the driver and witnesses to the police station for questioning. The official handed over the body to his mother for burial. The police department handled the driver according to the law. It is now heard that the police investigation concluded that the driver was not at fault and that the deceased was responsible for his own death, so he was not prosecuted and the driver was released. The deceased's mother felt aggrieved that her only son was tragically crushed to death and the driver was able to escape responsibility, so she expressed her dissatisfaction and planned to seek legal remedies on her own in the hope of punishment and compensation for damages.

Economic Special

How to Suppress Prices? 86

— I

This publication previously held a symposium on the issue of prices, and the profound discussions and grand proposals were widely noticed by all sectors of society. It is a pity that although there were concrete measures, they could not be effectively implemented, which is regrettable! Recently, the exchange rate has shrunk, and the trend of hoarding and speculation has become more intense, and prices have continued to rise, especially for necessities such as rice and coal. Not only has this caused problems for the salaried class, but even the general business community who have made a fortune from the national crisis may find it difficult to sustain themselves. This is truly a serious problem for the current society! In my opinion, the following methods should be adopted to suppress prices now in order to alleviate the immediate crisis:

(1) It is recommended that the central government allow those who purchase imported rice and coal and other necessities to settle foreign exchange at the exchange rate of seven pence per dollar quoted by the Chongqing Central Trust of China.

(2) It is recommended that the central government quickly order the Shanghai banking industry to notify all those who have mortgaged goods to purchase rice and coal and other necessities.

(3) It is recommended that the central government quickly order the Shanghai court to investigate and deal strictly with those who hoard and speculate in accordance with the law.

Regardless of the extent to which the above points can be implemented in reality, some measures are sufficient to warn unscrupulous merchants and reassure the people.

(4) Announce the names of unscrupulous merchants who hoard and speculate in newspapers so that they are subject to public opinion.

(5) Daily necessities such as rice and coal should be purchased collectively by various public groups and associations in conjunction with the Public Works Department, and stored in appropriate quantities. If funds are needed, they should be provided by the banking industry.

In short, although rising prices are a common phenomenon during wartime, a careful observation of the reasons for the rising prices in Shanghai and the severity of the rate of increase reveals that they are indeed manipulated by hoarders and speculators. There is no doubt that on the one hand, we should consider collective purchase of necessities, and on the other hand, we should also use the various methods mentioned above to make hoarders and speculators aware of the warning, and prices can be slightly suppressed! Otherwise, not only will it affect the increase in prices in the rear, but it will also be enough to cause problems for local public order. It is not just a matter of making the rich richer and the poor poorer. Readers should not dismiss these words as nonsense! (29, 2, 14)

Japan's Trade Surrounded on All Sides 87

— Xia Zhi

The Sound of Being Surrounded on All Sides - The Japanese financial clique government is exhausting all means to maintain the import of raw materials and military supplies. But everything has failed. European and American countries declared to them at the beginning of the Japanese invasion of China, "No cash, no supply!" Japan frantically shouted to revitalize exports, but the raw materials for export industries also need to be purchased with cash. Its means of production (machines, raw materials, fuel) and productivity (labor, power, capital) have also been seized by the military industry. Increasing production is impossible, so how can exports increase? So at first, they sent all their cash reserves, and after exhausting all means, they had to use the issuance reserves. The Japanese yen has long become a paper currency standard. So they had to sing the high tune of revitalizing exports again. But is it useful? According to the investigation by its Ministry of Commerce and Industry: its production index reached its peak in March of last year and then began to decline sharply. The manufacturing industry production index decreased sharply from 191.3% in March of last year to 173.2% in September; mining production also decreased sharply from 175.2% to 155%. Heavy industry decreased from 358.1% to 314.2%; electricity decreased from 193.9% to 173.7%; gas decreased from 160.8% to 136.5%; the overall index decreased from 189.3% to 171%. The production increase policy has completely failed, and export capacity has also failed. Desperate, they had to intensify their plunder of China; even depriving its people of their food and clothing. But the trade deficit with third countries last year still reached more than 460 million Japanese yen.

Now: labor shortages, financial shortages, and raw material shortages are all intensifying; fuel shortages and food shortages are particularly serious. Moreover, the United States is preparing to further implement a policy of embargoing arms to Japan after the expiration of the U.S.-Japan commercial treaty. Following this, the Franco-Japanese commercial treaty will also expire. Japan's trade environment is not only as bad as it is for the United States and France, but it is also in an extremely bad state for Britain, India, Australia, the Soviet Union, Germany, and Italy. The significance of this is not only to illustrate his isolated international status; more importantly, it is to point out that his economic power is rapidly collapsing; and to point out to European and American countries that "the time to implement economic sanctions against Japan" has matured. At the same time, it is also the prelude to the exhaustion of his war materials. Here, let's give a brief explanation of his trade environment!

No Treaty Status with the United States - In July last year, the U.S. Congress was enthusiastically discussing amending the Neutrality Act and dreaming of the Dreyfus Act; the White House resolutely revoked the U.S.-Japan commercial treaty. This was a sign that it had already decided to implement a ban on arms exports to Japan, and it was also used as preparation for implementing this policy. The U.S.-Japan commercial treaty expired on January 26 of this year; the two countries have entered a state of no treaty. The arms embargo against Japan has been put on the agenda; Japan's means of threats and inducements will never change America's determination. The loan bill to China has been passed by the Senate, which is another manifestation of the United States' economic sanctions against Japan and its assistance to China's resistance against Japan.

The United States is not only the main source of the arms and raw materials that Japan needs, but also has become the only source since the outbreak of the European War. At the same time, it is also the largest market for Japan to obtain export foreign exchange. Therefore, the beginning of the no-treaty status between the U.S. and Japan can be said to be the beginning of the severance of the supply of Japan's war economic power.

Franco-Japanese Commercial Treaty About to Expire - The Franco-Japanese commercial treaty signed on March 15 last year has a validity period of only one year; it will expire on the 15th of next month. Last year, Japan made a lot of profit from doing business in France and its colonies; its trade surplus reached more than one million pounds; and it purchased a large amount of military materials from France, a large amount of industrial salt from Tunisia, and a large amount of rubber and coal from Annam. These are all necessary materials for Japan's war. Japan is now trying to renew its contract with France, but France is ignoring it.

There are many reasons why France is unwilling to renew the commercial treaty with Japan. Politically, it is not only because it sympathizes with China's war of resistance; it will not forget that after the treaty was signed last year, Japan brutally promoted anti-British and anti-French movements in the Tianjin area, and it is still intensifying. Moreover, according to the agreement between France and Japan in 1907, both parties should help each other to ensure the peace and security of the Chinese region where French and Japanese territories border; but Japan is now completely disregarding this agreement; not only invading Hainan Island and its nearby Chinese territories, and engaging in military preparations for future attacks on French Indochina; but also repeatedly bombing the Yunnan-Vietnam Railway built by French capital. Therefore, the expiration of the Franco-Japanese commercial treaty is an opportunity for France to implement economic retaliation, how can it let it go lightly? Moreover, from an economic point of view; most of the materials France supplies to Japan are necessary equipment for France's war against Germany today, while what Japan supplies to France are just non-essential or even luxury goods such as salmon, pottery, and silk fabrics. In France today during wartime, it is precisely afraid of the import of such items. Therefore, there is no reason to renew the contract with Japan.

The Long-Abnormal Anglo-Japanese Trade - After the breakdown of the Anglo-Japanese cotton industry negotiations in 1934, the trade relations between Britain and Japan have long been abnormal. From the British point of view: there is no need to maintain trade with Japan. Because Japan's exports to the UK are mainly canned food, cotton silk fabrics, porcelain pottery, etc.; these all conflict with British industry. In the UK's trade with third countries, Japan accounts for only one to two percent. And it shows a constant trade deficit. But from the Japanese point of view; the relationship is extremely important. Japan's exports to the UK account for about 23.2% of total exports; imports from the UK account for about 22.8% of total imports. The main items imported from the UK are caustic soda, fuel, leather, animal hair, cotton and linen fibers and other raw materials. After Japan instigated the anti-British movement last summer, Britain considered means of economic retaliation against Japan. But Britain's actions still do not abandon its gentlemanly demeanor; although it has not formally implemented it on the surface, it has actually stopped maintaining trade relations with Japan. For example, in last year's total Japanese exports, Britain's position has dropped to 3.7%; in Japan's total imports, Britain's position has dropped to 0.9%.

Indo-Japanese Talks Completely Broken - India is the main market for Japanese cotton silk fabrics. At the same time, it is the main supplier of minerals such as iron and lead, and raw materials such as cotton, plant fibers, beans, and oil residues. Japan's exports of cotton fabrics to India not only hit the interests of the British Empire, but also harm the growth of India's emerging cotton spinning industry. Therefore, the Indo-Japanese cotton industry talks break down every time they are held. On November 10 last year, the third round of talks between India and Japan began again. At the beginning, India resolutely rejected Japan's opinions, and then launched a counterattack.

The demands made by Japan to India were (1) to reduce the current ad valorem tariff rate of 50% on cotton cloth imports; (2) to increase the quota for Japanese high-grade cotton cloth exports to India; (3) to revise the current cotton-cotton cloth exchange ratio system. India not only completely refused; but decided (1) never to reduce taxes, and prepare to increase them; (2) not to expand the import quota for high-grade Japanese cotton cloth, and plan to reduce it even further; (3) under the principle of not hindering the Indian cotton industry, it is okay to sell excess cotton to Japan. In this way, the Indo-Japanese talks completely broke down, and there is no possibility of reopening them to this day.

Australia's Economic Break with Japan - Japan needs a lot of wool, wheat, leather, lead, tin, etc. from Australia. However, Australia's thirst for industrial production materials from South Africa cannot be compensated by Japan. The cotton fabrics and canned food supplied by Japan are exactly the industries that Australia wants to operate on its own. Therefore, the Australian Labor Party has always been the vanguard of anti-Japanese sentiment. After the outbreak of the Sino-Japanese War, Australia launched an informal economic break with Japan. With the exposure of Japan's southward advance conspiracy today, this movement is expanding more actively.

The Soviet Union Ignores Japan's Demands - Although the Soviet Union is currently pursuing multi-faceted diplomacy, its relationship with Japan has always deteriorated. Recently, although there is a Japanese-Soviet fisheries agreement, it is only the result of Japan's submission to the Soviet Union. To obtain this agreement, Japan had to repay the Soviet Union all the money for purchasing the Chinese Eastern Railway. There are hundreds of pending disputes between Japan and the Soviet Union, and the issue of trade is one of them. Until now, there is no formal commercial treaty between Japan and the Soviet Union. However, the minerals, oil, timber, fur, etc. that Japan needs can be fully supplied by the Soviet Union. Around January 10 of this year, Japanese Ambassador to the Soviet Union Togo led Minister Songshima to Moscow, attempting to discuss this issue with the Soviet Union's People's Commissar for Foreign Trade, but the Soviet Union just ignored him.

The Nominal German-Japanese Commercial Treaty - Germany hastily concluded a commercial treaty with Japan last year. This is just a diplomatic gesture of Germany, with empty promises and no real benefit. Especially since the invasion of Poland expanded into the European War, Germany's foreign trade routes have been completely blocked by the British and French navies. Although Japan wants to collude with Germany through Soviet territory, Germany has no ability to supply Japan's military needs, and the Soviet Union is definitely unwilling to provide this convenient gateway. In the past, Japan obtained 40% to 50% of the machinery it needed from the United States; 25% to 30% from Germany; and 5% to 20% from Britain. Now that the U.S. and Japan have entered a state of no treaty, Britain and Germany are both unable to take care of themselves. The hope of obtaining supplies from overseas has been completely cut off so far.

Fundamentally Hostile Italo-Japanese Trade - Germany, as an international pariah, has always been at odds with Japan. Although the Italo-Japanese commercial agreement was signed in July of the year before last, it cannot help Japan's war economy at all. Both countries rely on the import of production materials and use light industrial products as their main exports. Therefore, in silk and silk fabrics, rayon and rayon fabrics, etc., they are in a hostile position in the world market. Having something in common is the main factor in promoting international trade relations, but it does not exist at all between Italy and Japan.

Concluding Remarks - In short: Japan's goods have no way out in the world market; the supply doors for the war materials and raw materials Japan needs are closing one by one. Its policy of aggression is backfiring. Therefore, hoping that the Japanese financial clique will repent is absolutely impossible. The only way to ensure the independent and free survival of the Chinese nation is to resolutely resist to the end; the only way to ensure the rights and interests of Europe and the United States is to provide economic aid to China and implement sanctions against Japan. Japan's trade environment has now fallen into a state of being surrounded on all sides, and Japan's war economy can be said to have reached the end of its rope.

From the Abolition of the U.S.-Japan Commercial Treaty to Sino-U.S. Economic Relations 88

— Yu Xielin

U.S. Relations with Japan

For fifty years, the United States has been deeply concerned about Far Eastern affairs, such as the convening of the Washington Conference in 1922; the Stimson Doctrine promoted by the United States after the "September 18th Incident"; and even more so since the outbreak of the Sino-Japanese War. The abolition of the U.S.-Japan commercial treaty on January 26 of this year can be said to be a manifestation of the United States' proactive Far Eastern policy.

The purpose of the United States in abolishing the U.S.-Japan commercial treaty is of course to maintain its interests in the Far East. Considering its past policies, it was the Open Door Policy. But today's situation in the Far East is no longer what it used to be. The Open Door Policy is in danger of being destroyed by the Japanese. How can the United States, in its current environment, take a listening attitude? The abolition of the U.S.-Japan commercial treaty is therefore the first step in the United States' proactive containment of Japan.

Reasons for Abolishing the Commercial Treaty

U.S. trade with Japan has consistently accounted for more than 40% of its total trade with the Far East; Japan exchanges silk and tea for U.S. cotton, steel, oil, etc., and in recent years the United States has had a huge trade surplus with Japan. So why did the United States abolish the U.S.-Japan commercial treaty? Without discussing the various political issues involved; in terms of economics, the main points that can be mentioned are as follows.

Today, most of China's market has been monopolized by the Japanese; Japan seizes China's rich raw materials, preventing them from being supplied to U.S. industrial needs; at the same time, it prevents U.S. surplus goods from being able to gain a foothold in the Chinese market. In the years before the war, the speed of increase in the trade volume between China and the United States was unmatched by other countries. The Americans cannot sit idly by and watch the Japanese rampage like this.

U.S.-Japan trade is very large and increases annually. However, what has increased is only military supplies. Since the outbreak of the European War, the U.S. military industry does not have to worry about finding a way out. In addition, the largest export to Japan is cotton, etc., but it has decreased a lot in recent years. There is also a plan to use as much Chinese cotton as possible to replace U.S. cotton. Therefore, the maintenance of U.S.-Japan trade is actually no longer profitable for the United States.

The United States has invested huge amounts of capital in the Far East, and after many years of operation, it has achieved its current position. However, under the wide-ranging destruction of the Japanese today, the businesses run by Americans have been greatly threatened. How can the Americans endure it?

Sino-U.S. Trade Relations

The abolition of the U.S.-Japan commercial treaty has a great relationship with China. Sino-U.S. trade has developed very rapidly in recent years. And there is an annual trade surplus. In today's wartime, although trade with the United States has decreased a lot, it still occupies an important position. The following is a record of the total trade volume between China and the United States in the most recent five years: (unit: thousands of yuan)

Exports to the United States Imports from the United States

Year 24 136,467 173,731

Year 25 186,321 185,522

Year 26 231,449 188,859

Year 27 86,853 151,154

Year 28 15,675 199,670

(Note) The total import and export volume for Year 28 is only from January to October.

China's exports to the United States are mainly tung oil, raw silk, eggs, and pig bristles. These are all major raw materials for American industry. Since the outbreak of the European War last fall, exports to the United States have increased sharply, and it is expected to restore the pre-war state, or even surpass it. As for the goods imported from the United States, machinery and minerals are the most important. Because our country needs a large amount of such goods in this war of resistance and nation-building, there is hope for a sharp increase in the future. As for cotton, because most of the domestic production has been seized, the Chinese and foreign yarn factories in Shanghai have to rely on foreign cotton, so the import of U.S. cotton is also increasing.

U.S. Investment in China

According to the U.S. Department of Commerce's estimate in 1935, U.S. investment in China was US$132 million. According to the U.S. Secretary of State Hull's estimate on January 10, 1938, it was US$240 million. Most of it is direct investment; securities investment is very small. According to Romer's estimate, in 1932, 32% of U.S. direct investment in China was in import and export businesses; 23% was in public utilities, including Shanghai's electricity company and telephone company; 17% was in banking and financial businesses, such as Citibank, Chase, and American Express; its activities were limited to trade-related finance in major commercial ports; 14% was in manufacturing, such as the cigarette industry, egg product manufacturing, and blanket industry; 7% was in transportation; 6% was in real estate; and 1% was in mining. Two-thirds of it is concentrated in Shanghai, and most of the rest is concentrated in Tianjin. Recently, in the field of aviation, American investment has greatly developed. For example, the China National Aviation Corporation, jointly operated by Pan American Airways and China. In November 1936, it extended the Pacific transoceanic route to complete the Sino-U.S. air link. Since the outbreak of the Sino-Japanese War, China has also sold all the properties of the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company in coastal ports to American merchants. But in general, the United States' investment in China is most substantial in cultural investment; the total amount of cultural investment is four times that of Britain, twice that of France, and 30 times that of Japan. Schools and hospitals run by old and new missions and American consortia are located throughout the country. The expenses of the churches in China amount to as much as US$6.4 million per year.

Sino-U.S. Monetary Agreement and Loan Relations

Starting in June 1934, the United States purchased large amounts of silver, so China's silver flowed out continuously, causing an unprecedented financial panic. China then implemented the legal tender policy on November 4, 1935, centralizing silver and purchasing it as state-owned. In order to stabilize the exchange rate of the legal tender, our authorities sold 50 million taels of silver to the United States at a price of US$0.65 per tael through the Central Bank. In February 1936, China purchased US$10 million worth of gold from the United States and deposited it in the Federal Reserve Bank of the United States. The Sino-U.S. Monetary Agreement was signed on May 18. In July 1937, the Sino-U.S. Monetary Agreement was signed for the second time. In today's wartime, the United States continues to purchase our silver. This move has greatly helped the promotion of our country's legal tender policy, so the Sino-U.S. relationship has become closer due to the monetary agreement.

The new loans from the United States to our government were only cotton and wheat loans before the war. During the war, we were loaned another 25 million yuan; according to recent reports, a new loan agreement has been established between China and the United States, and this action is actually a powerful assistance from the United States to enhance our war of resistance.

The United States first purchased our silver to stabilize the exchange rate of our legal tender; then loaned us huge sums of money to enhance our combat strength. Therefore, China and the United States have moved from being close to cooperation, jointly seeking peace in the Far East. The Americans deeply know that if our country wins, the United States' interests in the Far East can be preserved; otherwise, it will be driven out. Therefore, when our country is in difficulty, the Americans will do their best to help.

Since the U.S.-Japan commercial treaty was abolished, the United States' relationship with the Far East has entered a new stage. Japan's economic difficulties have become even more severe as a result.
