Wang Dan Kui Advocates Cherishing Rice 94

— Sun Choucheng

Mr. Wang Qingmu, styled Dan Kui, was a native of Chongming and a Jinshi (successful candidate in the highest imperial examinations) of the former Qing Dynasty, who served as a Lianfang (an official responsible for investigating and rectifying misconduct) and was admired by all for his integrity and fairness. At the age of eighty-one, his spirit was even more vigorous than ever. In view of the recent high price of rice in Shanghai, which was unprecedented, he earnestly advised people to cherish rice, as it concerns one of the four major elements of life: clothing, food, housing, and transportation. Therefore, what Mr. Wang said is recorded as follows:

Guanzi said, "The five grains are the people's lifeblood." He also said, "Of all things, the five grains are the most important." In ancient times, wise rulers valued the five grains over pearls and jade, which was passed down as a beautiful tale. Today, people treasure and hide a single hook of gold, yet they carelessly waste grains of rice, forgetting what they should value. Shanghai is a place where people from all directions gather, and the population is dense. Charitable people print and distribute good books, some of which include discussions on cherishing grain, but society does not pay much attention. The waste in restaurants and bars is beyond description, and even among the thousands of households, many arbitrarily discard rice. In the past, when the price of rice was low, people did not know to cherish it, and this became a habit. In the early years of the Guangxu reign, a stone of rice cost two thousand cash, but now it costs as much as fifty yuan per stone, with one yuan equal to three thousand cash, totaling one hundred and fifty thousand cash, which is seventy-five times higher. Cherishing rice should be done regardless of whether it is cheap or expensive; it should be cherished when it is cheap, and even more so when it is expensive. Why not pay attention to this and violate the ancient saying of treasuring grains of rice? A certain prime minister of the Song Dynasty, who sought power and accepted bribes, held sway both at home and abroad. His household had over a thousand people, who were tired of rich food. The kitchen happened to be next to a Buddhist monastery, and every day rice flowed into the ditch, looking like jade grains and pearl beads. The monks of the monastery, along with their novices, used bamboo baskets to scoop it up, wash it clean, and dry it in the sun. Besides feeding the monks, they accumulated thirteen storage bins. Later, the prime minister was found guilty and defeated, and his family members scattered. His widowed mother, over eighty years old, wandered to the capital, begging along the streets. One day, she arrived in front of the mountain gate of the monastery. The monk saw her, knew that she was the mother of the prime minister, and could not help but sigh. He then allocated a room for her to live in, and she ate with the monks at every meal, the rice being cooked from the dried rice in the storage bins. The mother soon fell ill and died, and was buried in a worn mat. Reflecting on this, I am deeply moved. The virtue of a child is the responsibility of the mother. In the "Family" hexagram of the Book of Changes, the woman is in charge of the food. The mother of the prime minister failed to educate her son and neglected her duties in managing the food, which led to the neglect of cherishing grain as the main cause of ruin. The tragic result is heartbreaking; shouldn't this be taken as a warning? The people of this country have always lacked research on diet and hygiene, so stomach diseases are particularly common. When eating rice, people neglect to chew properly, and after it enters the stomach, the nutrition is insufficient, easily leading to stagnation. Tao Yinjun's poem says, "When eating, avoid being too coarse and too fast; it is better to eat smaller meals in succession than to fill the stomach at once, as it harms the qi and injures the spleen." This is an excellent method of eating. School dining hall rules include the four words "chew slowly and swallow slowly," which shows genuine care for the students. Generally speaking, eating a bowl of rice that is chewed carefully is better than eating two bowls of rice swallowed whole. This is because rice that is chewed carefully is rich in nourishment and easy to digest, so it is beneficial to the human body, while rice swallowed whole is the opposite. Only those who pay attention to hygiene can distinguish this. Reducing the waste of rice at home, accumulating day by day, can save a lot. This is also a way to cherish rice. Madam Ouyang, the wife of Zeng Wenzhenggong, ascended to immortality after her death and was known as Fairy Ouyang. She once descended to the altar to instruct women to cherish the five grains, and attached a poem saying, "The world's customs are declining, alas, today; who still cherishes the five grains? I advise you women to be vigilant, lest you accumulate sins and bring disaster." Therefore, I especially address women. Today, the people of this country are suffering an unprecedented catastrophe. How should we cleanse our hearts and minds to reach the heavens? Cherishing rice is not just about saving money, but also about saving us from the catastrophe. May my compatriots have a sudden awakening at dawn.

A Week's Economical Menu 95

— Ms. Hua Ying

Since the beginning of the lunar new year, prices have soared. Each stone of foreign rice now costs fifty yuan, and Du rice even exceeds this number. The seven necessities of life have all increased dramatically, causing housewives to shake their heads and frown, truly suffering from the hardship of making ends meet. A year ago, this economical menu would have cost six or seven jiao (cents) and been enough for two meat dishes and two vegetarian dishes. Now, it costs more than one yuan, which is really too difficult. The other day, my family ate a very ordinary dish of stir-fried chives and bean curd sheets with shredded pork, which cost a huge seven jiao. The children still didn't eat their fill, and the housewife didn't dare to pick up her chopsticks. Alas, only those black-hearted hoarders and profiteers who speculate and get rich don't care about this level of living, while the rest of us who rely on salaries to live should just wait to die. Since "increasing income" is impossible, we can only start with "reducing expenditure." Every day, we must choose inexpensive ingredients for two meat dishes and two vegetarian dishes. If that is beyond our means, then eat one meat dish and two vegetarian dishes, or one meat dish and one vegetarian dish; please use your own discretion. At the same time, save on rice by having one rice meal and two porridge meals each day, and eat only enough to satisfy your hunger. In this time of living death, we can only tighten our belts and live one day at a time.

How to Protect Socks 96

— Zhao Bing

Although socks are a small item, if we are not careful in wearing them, the cost of socks in a year can be considerable.

So how should we protect them to make them last longer?

In addition to paying attention to whether there are any holes when buying them, the most important thing is to be careful ourselves. If there is a hole, we should immediately sew it up or attach a sock bottom. The sock toes and heels are the most prone to damage, because these are the areas where the foot exerts the most force when walking. However, as long as we are a little lazy, then, "A small hole not mended will lead to a big hole that causes suffering." A small hole will gradually spread to the entire sock, thereby reducing the sock's lifespan.

People with sweaty feet tend to wear out socks more often than people with less sweaty feet, simply because socks are easily damaged when they get wet. It's best to make a pair of cloth sock liners to wear inside the socks. I think that way, the number of socks used will definitely be reduced.

Washing socks frequently is also the best way to protect them, not only making them last longer, but also meeting hygiene requirements. However, many people mistakenly believe that washing them frequently will easily damage them. However, when washing them, do not use a brush to scrub them; rub them gently.

At a time when white goods are expensive, we should do our best to protect the socks we wear, so as to reduce the amount we need to wear.

Tianchu Recipes

(1) Stewed Four Happiness Meat (also known as Dongpo Pork) 97

Ingredients: One pound of streaky pork belly with three layers, five fen (1 fen = 0.1 ounce) of salt, a little monosodium glutamate (MSG), 1.3 liang (1 liang = 1.76 oz) of light soy sauce, six liang of Shaoxing wine, a large pot of natural water, 3-4 liang of rock sugar, one iron fork for grilling, one earthenware pot, a dozen pieces of broken porcelain, one yellow basket lid, one charcoal stove, several pounds of charcoal, one large stewing pot for stewing the meat.

Preparation: First, remove the hair from the pork, wash it clean, and cut it into two-inch squares. Then, put the oil, wine, etc., all into the large stewing pot. Then, rub the salt all over the pork. Use an iron fork to hold the pork over the charcoal fire until both sides turn yellow. Take it out and then place the porcelain pieces into the large stewing pot. Add the yellow basket lid and place the pork on top of the yellow basket lid. Stew it over the charcoal fire. After stewing it for forty or fifty boils, add six liang of Shaoxing wine. Wait for more than a hundred boils before adding natural water. The amount of water should cover the surface of the meat by more than two inches. After stewing until the pork skin turns red, add the rock sugar and stew for another three-quarters of an hour. Then, turn the meat over, add a little MSG, and stew for another three-quarters of an hour or so. Turn it over again, and so on, turning it over four or five times in a row until the meat flavor comes out and the pork skin is crispy.

When serving, the taste is endlessly delicious. Note: This recipe will be published every Monday in the "Clothing, Food, Housing, and Transportation" section. Readers are encouraged to collect them on schedule so that they can become a valuable recipe book in the future.

If you would like to purchase Ajinomoto, oil, salt, soy sauce, and vinegar, please call "44194" and a special delivery person will be sent to deliver them without any delivery fee.

Lantern Festival Food 98

— Qiu Lang

The Lantern Festival can be said to be the continuation of the Lunar New Year celebrations, and it is also the tail end of the Lunar New Year. Eating and entertainment are the most exciting parts of the New Year, and the Lantern Festival is no different. There is a saying: "Eat tangyuan (glutinous rice balls) at the beginning of the Lantern Festival, and eat rice cake at the end. Celebrate the Lantern Festival on the fifteenth of the first month." In the past, during peaceful times, setting up lanterns on the Yuan night (Lantern Festival) was the most organized and lively, as in the saying: "The golden crow is not forbidden, the city opens and does not sleep," but such joy can only be found in books now. In these days of serious national crisis, it is naturally out of the question. However, on this isolated island, perhaps there are still people who are perfunctorily going through the motions to embellish this good night.

According to Hangzhou custom, the thirteenth day of the first month is the Shangdeng (first lighting of the lanterns), and the seventeenth is the Luodeng (closing of the lanterns). As for other places, the twelfth is the Shangdeng, and the eighteenth is the Luodeng. This is due to different local customs. In addition to lantern competitions, there are seasonal foods for the Lantern Festival. The so-called Shangdeng tangyuan (also known as lantern tangyuan) is made by grinding glutinous rice into flour, mixing it with water, and making small balls the size of lotus seeds. They are cooked in boiling water until they are done, and then sprinkled with osmanthus sugar juice, making them fragrant and delicious. I remember that the poet Chen Xuyuan had a verse about tangyuan, saying: "After all, the daughters' hands are nimble, rouge and powder are used to make lantern tangyuan," what a beautiful and elegant verse! After the Shangdeng, there is the Yuanxiao (Lantern Festival), and there is also a kind of food called Yuanxiao, which is also made of rice flour and is the size of walnuts, with various fillings inside, such as red bean paste, white sugar, peach meat, and melon seeds. However, this product made in Beiping (Beijing) is the most famous, so the market often uses Beiping Yuanxiao as a selling point. By the time of the Luodeng, the festival ends with eating rice cake. The various foods listed above are all cooked in the family during the Shangdeng time each day, first offered to the ancestors, and then eaten together by the family, thus ending the eating part of the Lunar New Year.

A Small Record of Dietary Nourishment

Chinese Cabbage 99

— Zhang Jingren

Chinese cabbage is also called song. Lu Dian's "Pi Ya" says that it wilts late in the winter and is often seen with a green stalk, so it is called song. Li Shizhen said that there are two types, one with a round stalk, slightly green and thick, and one with a white stalk, thin and flat, which is what is commonly seen in kitchens today. As for the yellow bud cabbage, it is also a variation of Chinese cabbage, especially because it is produced in different places, grown differently, and has different soil qualities, so its properties and tastes are also different. As for its effects, according to various herbal books, it is warm in nature, sweet in taste, non-toxic, promotes intestinal movement, relieves worries, harmonizes the middle and lowers the qi, helps digestion, relieves alcohol, treats miasma, and stops hot coughs. It is especially good for winter sweating, because after frost, its nature turns cool and its taste becomes sweeter. Therefore, mashing raw cabbage can treat sores and poison, and using the juice to focus on the eyes can remove pterygium. Western medicine uses it to make ointments as a soothing and calming agent, saying that its effects can replace opium, and it can also induce perspiration, promote urination, and cause mild diarrhea. When taken with maritime onion and foxglove, it can treat bloating. Its seeds can be squeezed for oil, which can grow hair and prevent rust when applied to knives and swords, so the gun oil used by the military is cabbage seed oil. However, "Rihua Zhujia Bencao" says that it is cool in nature and slightly poisonous, and eating too much can cause skin itching. However, people today use it as a common food, and this has never been seen. Generally, what Rihua refers to is the yellow bud cabbage, a variation of Chinese cabbage. Because it is grown in sandy soil, its properties are different from those grown in clay soil. Li Shizhen said: "Yellow bud cabbage is cultivated by northerners using horse manure, imitating the method of growing yellow chives." So, the ancient saying "early chives in early spring, late song in late autumn" refers to the secret of growing variations of crops, not the common crops in general. Horse manure contains nitrates, which have the unique property of rising and permeating. It is the same as the ammonium nitrate in imported fertilizers, so it can help the stems and leaves grow and become fully enlarged. The "Rihua Zi" says that it can cause skin wind, which is due to this reason. Therefore, I believe that those who are sensitive to irritating foods should avoid yellow bud cabbage, not Chinese cabbage. In terms of nourishment, those with more protein are considered valuable. Protein is nitrate, and ammonia is composed of nitrate and hydrogen, so yellow bud cabbage is more potent than Chinese cabbage. People with pale faces and thin bodies are caused by a lack of protein-containing foods, hence the saying "a face with cabbage color." Southerners are weaker than northerners, and even the meat color on the faces of the poor can be used to distinguish this, probably because the vegetables they eat are different. The nourishing power of cabbage seed oil and soybean oil can also be used to distinguish them. Those in charge of the food should pay close attention to this.

The Connection Between Clothes and Wives 100

— Jing Shusen

Everyone knows that clothes are what everyone needs to wear and cannot be separated from the body; and wives are what everyone needs to have, as "Of the three unfilial acts, having no descendants is the greatest." However, these are fundamentally two different things that are completely unrelated.

However, people in ancient times often liked to mention these two things together, as if they had a related relationship. Of course, if we seriously examine this, there must be many examples. Here, I will only cite a few of the most popular and common ones to prove this.

Those who have read the Romance of the Three Kingdoms probably remember that Mr. Liu once said: "Wives are like clothes, brothers are like limbs." The metaphor is wonderful and quite interesting. Unfortunately, his following two sentences: "Clothes that are torn can still be mended; limbs that are broken cannot be reconnected," although are his words of loyalty and righteousness, are a bit too dismissive of wives, aren't they?

The above passage is just a metaphor and does not directly establish any related relationship. Like in the Peking opera "Wujia Po," there is a duet between Wang Baochuan and her husband Xue Pinggui: "I asked him... if his clothes were torn?" Besides inquiring about her husband's diet and living conditions, she is also concerned about her husband's clothes. This clearly tells people that it is a wife's duty to care about her husband.

In fact, when a man marries a wife, his purpose is not solely for the problem of clothes; but many people always use the big issue of clothes as a guise to cover up his unspeakable shame. It is both dignified and grand, and can be considered the ultimate in speaking skills.

If you don't believe me, you can walk to any road or any street corner, and you will always hear a plaintive song: "Wang Laowu, Wang Laowu... lived for thirty-five years in vain, no one mends his torn clothes!..." This song is Wang Laowu expressing his inner suffering. Someone said: "If you haven't married, just say it straightforwardly. Why beat around the bush and say that your clothes are torn and no one mends them? Moreover, there are many issues concerning wives, so why specifically mention clothes?" This is based on what? I, the author, am not smart enough and await the guidance of someone more enlightened!

Finally, I recall an interesting and funny story that I heard in my childhood. Now, I will write it here, both for the readers to laugh at and as the conclusion to this article. It is said that there was once the son of a poor scholar who was nearing the age of thirty and had not yet married, and he was quite dissatisfied with his father. One day, he came up with a wild idea and wrote two five-character lines of poetry in a place that his father passed by every day: "At the age of twenty-five, clothes are torn and no one mends." Sure enough, the next day there was a response: "If you want someone to mend your clothes, wait another twenty-five!" He almost burst his stomach with anger. He immediately picked up his pen and wrote two seven-character lines of poetry: "It is rare for people to live to seventy in ancient times, who marries a wife at fifty?" He was confident and reasoned powerfully in this rebuttal, thinking that he would definitely achieve the final victory. Little did he know that his father was determined and lightly replied with two lines: "Taigong met King Wen at eighty, what's wrong with waiting a few more years, Father?"

Spring and Autumn

A Letter from a Small Temple Keeper 101

— Li Xingru

Since Shanghai became an "isolated island," it is said that temples and monasteries have also experienced a "prosperous" phenomenon. When life is being crushed to the point of suffocation, seeking divination is already extremely foolish, let alone feeding a group of social parasites. Below is a letter from a small temple keeper. For those foolish women who want to ask the bodhisattva to solve their fate, please take the time to read this passage. (Editor)

(1) Work: Every day, work starts from 6:00 AM to 10:00 PM before one can rest, for a total of fourteen hours of work. If there are Taoist ceremonies or meritorious deeds, working all night is also common. The scope of work includes all the affairs in the temple, non-stop work, and also serving the abbot in all private matters, serving in multiple roles, even worse than a slave.

(2) Treatment: In addition to providing food and lodging, the temple keeper's monthly salary ranges from one yuan to four or five yuan. If there are fasting ceremonies or Taoist performances, he can get some small rewards from the guests. However, if the reward exceeds one yuan, it must be handed over to the abbot, who will give back three or four jiao, and the rest will go into his own pocket.

(3) Meals: Although the abbot is a monk, he cultivates his mind but not his mouth. He cannot eat without chicken, meat, and fish, but his subordinates must be vegetarian and not allowed to eat meat. The abbot must have a meal of black rice in addition to white rice - a smoking habit. Such a monk is truly regrettable!

(4) Snobbery: In addition, he has a snobbish eye. If he sees a wealthy gentleman or a devout Buddhist coming, he will be extremely attentive and hospitable. If he encounters ordinary incense-burning guests, he will be greeted by Taoist priests. If he doesn't get much benefit, he will haggle over every penny, truly a snobbish person.

(5) Extortion: The means of extorting money are extremely clever and meticulous, taking tens of gold at every turn for doing good deeds. If Taoist priests are hired to chant mantras, the guests pay four yuan, but the Taoist priests only get thirty-eight cents. In addition, candle oil is also the biggest source of profit. If a guest burns incense, he is persuaded to buy large candles. As soon as the guest leaves, the candle is immediately pulled out. The market price of candle oil can sell for eighty to one hundred yuan per load. There are also various ways to extort money, with clever means, which are simply innumerable.

The above are all facts, witnessed and handled personally. Such monks are of no benefit to the country and only harm society. Now, I will reveal the inside story one by one, hoping that kind-hearted and sincere believers will use their useful money to help the refugees in need and not do this foolish act again.

Another Charitable Hospital 102

— Wei Cheng

After reading the article "American Refugee Hospital" by Ruo Mengjun in the first issue of this month's magazine, I couldn't help but think of another hospital dedicated to benefiting the poor and sick.

This hospital is located in a Western-style house near the intersection of Wangzhi Road and Luba Road in the French Concession. There is no nameplate in front of the door. As far as I know, I heard that it is run by a German "Tong Sheng Miss", presumably a member of the church who specializes in charitable work, so people commonly call it "Tong Sheng Hospital". The hospital has two clinics, one for men and the other for women. There are more than a dozen German doctors and Chinese assistants in the hospital, all of whom are women. Here, in addition to not charging for medical expenses, the registration fee is also waived. The hospital also has both internal and surgical departments and has hospital wards.

The "American Refugee Hospital" is in West Shanghai, and some people may think it is inconvenient because it is far away. Then, you might as well go there, but please note: their consultation time is only in the morning, and the door is closed in the afternoon to avoid running into trouble.

Schools Should Not Charge for "Entry and Exit Permits" 103

— Ji Fufang

We often see in the newspapers that kidnappers mix into elementary schools, strip children of their clothes, or seduce young children and try to abduct them. For the safety of their children, most parents, regardless of the trouble, enter the school to pick up and drop off their children, either in person or by sending a servant.

Elementary school buildings are very small and naturally cannot accommodate these "idlers," but they cannot prevent parents from picking up and dropping off their students. And there are still irrelevant people entering and exiting, so recently many schools have issued "entry and exit permits" to restrict access.

The so-called "entry and exit permit" is a piece of paper card. Anyone who wants to receive it must pay between five jiao and one yuan, and a few schools say they will return it later, but most do not.

Amidst the rising tuition and book fees, the school authorities do not seem to be charging for "entry and exit permits". If necessary, only the cost of the permit can be charged, whether it is returned or not, as it increases the burden on parents, which is something the school authorities should pay attention to.

"Entry and exit permits" are a good method, but "everything costs money" is too "commercialized"!

Public Opinion Sanctions! 104

— Yan Zheng

The recent surge in prices is indeed too alarming, especially for rice, flour, and coal briquettes. Not to mention that the poor who spend a few jiao a day on retail purchases cannot survive, even those who rely on meager salaries are groaning and complaining. Everything else can be saved, but rice, flour, and coal stoves cannot be avoided. It is reported that the Municipal Federation sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to quickly find ways to stabilize prices, which is indeed the most pressing need. I think that if the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Public Works Department jointly organize a price balancing association to regulate prices, the results would definitely be very significant.

Considering the recent surge in rice, flour, and coal briquettes, the "unsmooth supply" and "sudden increase in water fees" cannot be ignored, but the main reason is still due to the reckless actions of unscrupulous speculators, which can be seen from the advertisements of several coal briquette factories urging delivery. Therefore, I believe that in addition to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Public Works Department jointly organizing a price balancing association, we must also launch "public opinion sanctions" to remedy the shortcomings of the balancing association.

The so-called "public opinion sanctions," as I have thought of them, include the following two, and I especially call on the editors of the newspapers to give their sympathy and support:

(1) The newspapers should publish as many articles as possible exposing the conspiracies of speculators.

(2) The editors of the newspapers (especially the supplements) should do their best to lead public opinion sanctions, set an example, and write more articles attacking or exposing speculators.

Rain After Clearing 105

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Twenty: Global Communication, Universal Language, Educational Awards for Talented Children

Ye Songfen said, "I don't believe it! Is it really possible that the newspaper delivery person looks like Jiang Jingrong? I'll go see for myself tomorrow, and then I'll understand." Old Zhang Ma said, "Young master! You must get up earlier tomorrow and let me stop him, then you can come out and see him. If you don't stop him first, he runs so fast, you'll never catch him. He almost got away today too, luckily I chased him quickly and caught him." Upon hearing this, Ye Songfen became even more suspicious that it was Jiang Jingrong, remembering that he ran faster than him during the school's Class A race. The next day, Ye Songfen indeed got up early, wanting to see the newspaper delivery person next door. He instructed Old Zhang Ma to call him when he arrived. When Jiang Jingrong arrived at the same old time to deliver the newspaper, Old Zhang Ma, while calling her young master, said to Jiang Jingrong, "Little newspaper delivery boy! Deliver slowly! Our young master wants to say a few words to you, wait a moment;" Jiang Jingrong, upon hearing this, thought, what does he mean, his young master wants to talk to me? Isn't his young master Ye Songfen? He took off running. But Ye Songfen had already chased after him. This time, Ye Songfen ran faster than him. Why? Because Ye Songfen was empty-handed, while he was carrying a large bundle of newspapers. Ye Songfen circled around in front of him and saw that it was indeed Jiang Jingrong. He said, "Jiang Jingrong! I've caught you today! I've written you several letters, but you never replied. What's the reason for that? I guessed that you didn't go to school anymore, but why are you selling newspapers?" Jiang Jingrong's face turned red, and he lowered his head without saying a word. Ye Songfen said, "We are good friends, why didn't you tell me? If you can't afford to go to school, I can help you. I've talked to my father, and he would definitely be willing to cover your tuition. Even if my father is not willing, I still have some savings in a bank account, and I can help you. Didn't we read in our textbook the saying, 'Friends should share their wealth'? Come to my house at five o'clock this afternoon, and we'll discuss a solution, okay? Once we've discussed it, you won't have to sell newspapers anymore." Jiang Jingrong shook his head and said, "No! It's better for me to sell newspapers. It's not that I don't want to study, don't want to go to school. But my mother gave birth to three of us, and you know I have two younger sisters. Because I was studying, my two sisters were forced to not be able to study. Now that I'm not studying, my eldest sister has already entered elementary school. So, I'm very happy in my heart, and I plan to let my youngest sister also enter school. I sell newspapers to help my mother, and my mother is really too hardworking for us children." As he spoke, he couldn't help but shed tears. (239)
